  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_11ffa7d9-faed-47ef-80d1-97e504d0ffa3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText16733917475122011093" style="display:none"><b>Sometimes you don't wake up. But if you happen to, you know things will never be the same.</b><br /><br />Three lives, three different paths to the same destination: Aspen Springs, a psychiatric hospital for those who have attempted the ultimate act—suicide.<br /><br />Vanessa is beautiful and smart, but her secrets keep her answering the call of the blade.<br /><br />Tony, after suffering a painful childhood, can only find peace through pills.<br /><br />And Conner, outwardly, has the perfect life. But dig a little deeper and find a boy who is in constant battle with his parents, his life, himself.<br /><br />In one instant each of these young people decided enough was enough. They grabbed the blade, the bottle, the gun—and tried to end it all. Now they have a second chance, and just maybe, with each other's help, they can find their way to a better life—but only if they're strong and can fight the demons that brought them here in the first place.</span>

<div id="review_1753586778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753586778" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753586778?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who support conversion therapy :)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=what-is-this-mess">what-is-this-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2015">z-read2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753586778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14037839888742114192">I started <i>Impulse</i> with really high hopes for this after enjoying Hopkins' <i>Tricks</i> series. Unfortunately, <i>Impulse</i> is a pretty terrible book, with severe issues of mental health being tackled sort of horribly and a shitty love triangle no one cares about. And besides that, it contains the most homophobic storyline I have ever had the displeasure of reading. I am not joking or exaggerating when I say <b>this storyline genuinely reads like someone's conversion therapy manifesto.</b> <br/><br/>Let's talk. <br/><br/>✔ <b>Before you</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14037839888742114192" style="display:none">I started <i>Impulse</i> with really high hopes for this after enjoying Hopkins' <i>Tricks</i> series. Unfortunately, <i>Impulse</i> is a pretty terrible book, with severe issues of mental health being tackled sort of horribly and a shitty love triangle no one cares about. And besides that, it contains the most homophobic storyline I have ever had the displeasure of reading. I am not joking or exaggerating when I say <b>this storyline genuinely reads like someone's conversion therapy manifesto.</b> <br /><br />Let's talk. <br /><br />✔ <b>Before you call me an SJW keyboard warrior so you can feel morally vindicated in your opinion:</b> Please at least read the damn review? I'm not complaining about this just for the sake of complaining or whatever you'd like to believe. This isn't some kind of minor "negative tropes" thing. If I had less self-confidence, I genuinely cannot imagine how I would've taken this and where this book could've taken me. Like, feel free to love this book – books are always subjective. But please do let me despise this book in peace. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>🌺 IT'S REALLY JUST NOT A QUALITY BOOK</u>
</b> <br /><br />Okay, this is the section where I'm a bitter salty person and I feel the need to explain why this book is just kind of generally bad ignoring all the stuff that is Problematique. Because that's who I am! Basically, it's super fucking obvious that this book wasn't outlined well or like, at all. <b>Each one of the characters goes through so many terrible events that Hopkins cannot possibly resolve them all</b>. She took on too many issues with only three characters, and it quickly approached a point where <b>she didn't even bother exploring these important issues in an inoffensive way.</b><br /><br />In terms of character, I had some major issues as well. All these characters could've been redeemable, but they're really not fleshed out? I'm not sure anyone ever told Ms. Hopkins that <b>trauma is not a character trait.</b><br /><br />✔ Vanessa has bipolar and kind of a judgemental asshole. That's it. I could've excused her bad behavior if she were redeemed, but she's not developed or fleshed-out, and she never really improves. <br />✔ Connor is a complete fuckboy and again, I could've excused it, but he's not fleshed-out. He's just boring and annoying. <br />✔ Tony's a decent character. Again, he's not fleshed-out <i>quite enough</i>, but he's a good guy. We'll talk about his arc later. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>🌺 MENTAL HEALTH IS SUPER, SUPER ROMANTIC</u>
</b><br /><br />✔ I don't think Hopkins did her research on mental health facilities. Every adult in this facility was either a villain or incompetent. Again, this is a toxic message to teens who want to help their own issues. Mental health facilities can be toxic places, yes, but they can also be great rehabilitation centers. Sticking with a negative view of rehabilitation places in every book strikes me as a bad message. This can be realistic on some occasions, it just didn't seem like the greatest plot decision. <br /><br />✔ <b>Suicide should not be used as a plot device.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Connor dies essentially so Tony and Vanessa can get together without feeling bad. His death is an easy way to get tears from the audience, but the constant use of suicide simply to get tears seems incredibly insensitive to mentally ill people. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Do depressed people need stories about how they are doomed to commit suicide anyway, despite their attempts to get better? I don't speak for all depressed people, but reading a book like this or <i>All the Bright Places</i> in a really depressed phase would've been extremely toxic for me. <b>“You eventually will commit suicide” is a very bleak message to give teens who feel their very existence is bleak.</b><br /><br />✔ <b>
  <i>I'll never stop cutting, lithium or no lithium. Only love can make me stop.</i>
</b><br />I saw this quote in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918354321?book_show_action=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Octavia's awesome review</a>, and I had to look it up because I almost didn't believe it. I'd forgotten how bad this was. <b>Love is positioned as a cure for mental illness.</b> Trust me, romantic love can't cure depression. <br /><br />✔ There's also this whole undertone of “our illness makes us better” running through the book. I really don't feel like complaining about this because so many other books have this same exact message, but I have <a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com/2017/06/13/book-chat-trauma-narratives-in-ya/" rel="nofollow noopener">a post about this</a> on my blog, if anyone's interested in general thoughts on this topic. <br /><br />✔ Generally, I feel like this isn't a book for mentally ill teens. I feel like it's a book for neurotypical teens who want to feel like their life doesn't suck. <br />There's a quote from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204068832?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> that I think sums it up best. <br /><b>
  <i>This book would be great to read if you think your life's shit. No matter how bad it gets for you, these kiddies have it so much worse. And if you think your life's worse than this, I recommend writing to Hopkins as you'll probably feature in her next book.</i>
</b><br />That's... well. It's just that these books don't portray the reality of being depressed or bipolar, to me. <b>They portray the horror of it all in this way that's meant to shock you, without actually interacting or talking about mental illness in a productive way.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>🌺 GAY CONVERSION IS NOT A GOOD FUCKING THING</u>
</b><br /><br />So here's probably my biggest issue with the book. <br /><b>
  <i>My lifestyle has caused me a lot of pain. I hope to change that when I get out of here.</i>
</b><br />This doesn't look too bad; Tony has been a prostitute, so that's probably what he's referring too, right? Well, no. He's actually specifically referring to being gay here. <br /><br />Let me repeat that: <b>his "gay lifestyle" caused him pain.</b> His gay "lifestyle." Caused him pain.<br /><br /><b>His redemption is becoming straight.</b><br /><br />I cannot begin to explain how harmful "positive character development in the form of learning you're actually straight" is. A narrative implying sexual assault caused him to believe he is gay, implying that had he not been gay, he wouldn't have been sexually assaulted as much, is <b>victim blaming</b> and absolutely disgusting. <br /><br />The idea of a gay character “realizing he's straight” has some kind of gross connotations in the first place and I don't think most straight authors have the nuanced understanding of queer experience to tackle it, but it is <i>technically</i> a thing that can happen to people. It's also <i>technically</i> likely he'd just realize he was bi, not that the possibility is ever mentioned. It's a lot rarer than homophobes would like to believe, and it's far rarer than straight people realizing they're actually gay, little as said straight people would like to believe. (I'm kidding. Mostly.) But the entire sexuality-change storyline is portrayed in an incredibly homophobic way here. It genuinely reads like fucking anti-gay propaganda. It is disgusting and it is horrifying to read. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>🌺 FINAL THOUGHTS AND A WRAP-UP</u>
</b><br /><br />Again, and I feel like a broken record at this point: <b>Hopkins' prose is great, and I like that she's trying to speak to teens without mincing words. However, she needs to stop stereotyping neuroatypical and lgbtq people.</b> She's not being great and representing us. She's being shitty. I can feel her fucking disdain for me through her pages and I'm so, so tired of it. I really wish I hadn't given her another chance. <br /><br />And again, this review isn't meant to be an attack on <i>you</i>. The book is in places well-written, exceedingly emotionally manipulative, and who knows, maybe Vanessa's storyline resonated with some readers. But I'd really ask anyone who's recommending this to consider the storyline for themselves and really, genuinely consider the canon of the book. Because <b>this is really gross.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14037839888742114192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1918354321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918354321" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1918354321?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416903574" href="/book/show/3330058-impulse">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who like emotional manipulation and mental illness used for shock value :)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1918354321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5504504370906964422"><u>
  <b>Why <i>Impulse</i> is the WORST Book I’ve Ever Read</b>
</u><br/><br/>Warning: This review will contain unmarked spoilers!<br/>Also, if you loved this book and are going to be angry if someone didn’t like it, you may want to keep scrolling.<br/><br/>Oh boy. Where to start... <br/><br/>This is my second time reading this book. <b>The first time was about a year ago, and it has stuck with me as one of the worst books I’ve ever read.</b> I decided I wanted to do a reread as more of an in-depth analysis, looking for the problematic aspects I picked up </span>
  <span id="freeText5504504370906964422" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>Why <i>Impulse</i> is the WORST Book I’ve Ever Read</b>
</u><br /><br />Warning: This review will contain unmarked spoilers!<br />Also, if you loved this book and are going to be angry if someone didn’t like it, you may want to keep scrolling.<br /><br />Oh boy. Where to start... <br /><br />This is my second time reading this book. <b>The first time was about a year ago, and it has stuck with me as one of the worst books I’ve ever read.</b> I decided I wanted to do a reread as more of an in-depth analysis, looking for the problematic aspects I picked up on the first time around.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br />The story follows three teens who have found themselves in Aspen Springs Psychiatric Hospital, each having recently attempted suicide. Conner is a golden boy with a bright future, Tony has spent much of his life in juvie and on the streets, and Vanessa lives in the shadow of her mother’s mental illnesses.<br /><br />I have this picture in my head of Ellen Hopkins sitting at her computer, trying to come up with her next novel idea. All of a sudden, it hits her! <b>Why not make a list of all the horrible things that could happen and try to incorporate it into one book?<br /><br />Issues that are involved in this book:</b><br />Suicide by gun<br />Parents pressuring children to be perfect<br />Parents with mental illness<br />Parents who neglect their children<br />Parents who abuse their children<br />Molestation of young children<br />Rich kid problems<br />Juvenile detention<br />Drugs - literally all of them - weed, heroin, meth, crystal<br />Suicide by drugs<br />Cutting<br />Sexuality<br />Suicide by cutting<br />Mental health facilities<br />Bipolar Disorder<br />Schizophrenia<br />Teacher/student relationships<br />Homophobia<br />AIDS<br />Veteran parents<br />Use of medication<br />Parental suicide<br />Abortion<br />Murder<br /><br />And those are only the major ones. This list is long, if you didn’t notice. <b>Far too long of a list of complex issues for an author to deal with and execute well in one novel.</b><br /><br />Each of these subjects deserve care and consideration when being written about, but most of them are either barely touched on or dealt with poorly. <b>It came off as if the author wanted to cram as many issues as she could into the book simply for shock value.</b><br /><br />From the interviews with Hopkins that I have read, this book is not own voices, and it shows. <b>Hopkins talks in all of her interviews about how she needs to write for teens because their lives are so complex and whatever, yet she obviously does not understand teens in the slightest.</b> More on that later.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br />The thing is, this book actually doesn't start off that bad, but I think that's what makes me hate this book so much. I actually went in thinking I was going to like it, whereas books that are shit from page one I don't expect anything out of.<br /><br /><b>Most of the writing is good, quite good even.</b> There are some passages about death and depression that do feel real. The verse is fine, though I think the verse just serves to reinforce the emotional manipulation with those oh-so-dramatic indentations.<br /><br />But the writing falters with Hopkins’s weird ass descriptions. <b>Ellen Hopkins has no idea how human beings talk to each other, let alone teenagers. The dialogue is frickin’ weird.</b> Such as:<br /><blockquote><i>"Voices. Strange faces. <b>A witches' stewpot of spells</b>."</i> Yup, a teenage boy would totally say ‘a witches' stewpot’.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Nothing about her hints nymph or flirt. She's a bulldog."</i>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"Shit happens...and my shit literally hit the fan."</i> Ellen Hopkins does not understand the meaning of the word ‘literally’.</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"Part of it is my old self, wanting nectar from a flower, the beat of a new heart."</i> Puh-leez. Like anyone thinks like this.</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"...an ice princess mom who raised me with glass kisses."</i> Oh, come on. You expect me to believe this guy, who was talking about orgasms a page ago, thought up this metaphor?</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"She doesn't even blink. Even a female dog wants her puppies clean and wrinkle-free—unless, of course, she's a Shar Pei."</i> This is the quote meant to illustrate how Conner's mother is an evil bitch, but honestly if someone said this to me I would fall over laughing out of sheer confusion.</blockquote><br />Perhaps this sort of writing is an attempt to make the story more dramatic. You tell me. I just think it sounds weird.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Oversexualization</u>
</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"A woman like that will work like clay—soften her up, touch her just right, the sculptor is guaranteed to have his way."</i>
</blockquote><br />The oversexualization of teenagers in this book is ridiculous. Yes, some teens are crazy horny but these guys are unrealistically gross.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I've got her right where I want her—on her knees, my hands caught in her silky blond hair as she whispers, I want you, Conner. Let me chase away your thought of your Emily. Come to me when you get out of this place. I'll show you how a real woman makes love to men such as you, and I don't give a damn how high the stakes are."</i>
</blockquote><br />This may shock you, but not all teens are obsessed with sex. <b>The oversexualization here is just a lazy attempt to make her characters sound like teens. It's uncomfortable and actually kind of insulting.</b><br /><blockquote><i>"...acting too tough to tumble. He's a nutshell asking to crack. Wonder if he's ever let a guy touch that pumped-up bod."</i> Just makes the character sound like a perv.</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"Did she have a clue that all those dollars spent on haute couture allowed her sweet young son to <b>feed his appetite for carnal pleasure—to divvy himself among a stable of fillies</b>?"</i> I actually feel gross reading that sentence. I'm supposed to sympathize with this character? And she actually thinks a teenage boy would say this? Or even an actual person of any age?</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Misrepresentation of Mental Health Facilities</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>This book shows a mental health facility as completely incompetent. They don't help the characters at all.</b><br /><br />Books about mental health should make an effort to show or even imply good relationships between the teens and therapists and those trying to help them, because many teens reading books like these are struggling with similar issues.<br /><br />All adults but one in the novel are absolutely horrific. <b>It does not encourage those going through similar things to seek help from adults and professionals, which is such a missed opportunity.</b><br /><br />Let's not even talk about the fucking "level four wilderness camp". <b>Please explain to me what mental health facility would think it's a good idea for their final test to be taking the “formerly” suicidal teenagers hiking ON A FUCKING CLIFF?! What did they think was going to happen?</b><br /><br />But that aspect is just part of the Ellen Hopkins trademark overdramatic-shock-value-books. All it does is piss me off.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Though this is a long book (666 pages, lol) the characters still feel underdeveloped.</b> Things could have been delved into with more depth. Perhaps this was due to the verse?<br /><br /><b>Conner:</b> He could have been a sympathetic character, but he actually ended up sounding kind of creepy. He comes off as manipulative, jealous, judgemental, homophobic, and rude. His thoughts are gross and often revolve around sex. He mocks the other patients dealing with mental illness. Yet we are meant to sympathize with him…<br /><br /><b>Tony:</b> He’s a nice guy. I liked Tony, really. He was the most interesting of the three. More on him in a bit.<br /><br /><b>Vanessa: Vanessa is a complete special snowflake.</b> She thinks she's ugly but all the guys fawn over her and constantly tell her how beautiful and amazing she is. She's actually incredibly boring compared to the other main characters.<br /><br />Suddenly, in the last 40 pages or so, Vanessa reveals she had an abortion previously. Vanessa's abortion plot is so pointless. It's brought up once near the very end and never talked about again. Why was it even included? We got no hints of it in her perspective and nothing about how it impacted her. Missed opportunity.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Tony’s Sexuality</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Tony starts off the story confident in his sexuality, until he suddenly realizes he was only gay because he was sexually abused and "turns straight".<br /><br />This is so problematic I hardly know where to start.</b><br /><br />Tony talks about how he thinks perversion is a result of being a target of perversion and then says he doesn't think he is gay, implying that his being gay was a result of being sexually abused.<br /><br />Yes, I know Ellen Hopkins isn't homophobic, I’ve read other stuff by her. <b>However, this book reinforces the idea that gay people are gay because there is something wrong with them, and that being gay is a form of perversion.<br /><br />The story also implies that Tony needed to realize he was straight in order to recover.</b><br /><br />It also reinforces that people who have been sexually abused are somehow broken or damaged or worse—likely to be perverted.<br /><blockquote><i>"Tony says he's gay and I'm guessing he really believes it, but he doesn't seem that way to me."</i> Like you have any fucking idea or right to judge someone's sexuality, Conner.</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>"It [being gay] doesn't mean that to me, Vanessa. My lifestyle has caused me a lot of pain. I hope to change that when I get out of here."</i> This is Tony actually implying that being gay is a cause of pain. <b>I can't get over how his storyline of redemption is a storyline basically where he is cured of being gay.</b></blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"It's so new, this woman thing, yet it doesn't feel foreign. It feels like where I've always belonged."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Romanticization of Mental Illness</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Not only is this book just a thinly veiled love triangle, but it is also one of the worst cases of romanticizing mental illness that I have ever read.</b> Here:<br /><blockquote><i>"Vanessa and Tony—two fractured people, <b>healed (perhaps) by unforeseen, not to mention unlikely, love</b>."</i> Oh Jesus fucking Christ! Implying that people who deal with mental illness are broken by calling them fractured <i>and</i> literally saying they were healed by love?!</blockquote><br /><b>The only characters that recover do so through falling in love, which reinforces that love is a cure for mental illness and the only way to recover is to fall in love romantically. Man, am I tired of reading that shit.</b><br /><blockquote><i>"I'll never stop cutting, lithium or no lithium. <b>Only love can make me quit.</b>"</i> If that doesn't prove this book romanticizes mental illness I don't know what will. The main character blatantly says that love is the only thing that can cure her.</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b><br /><br />Don’t get me wrong, I've thought a lot about why this book is so highly rated. I think people get caught up in the overdramatized style, the emotional manipulation, and the pure shock value and it gets mistaken for good writing. In the end, a lot of people miss these issues because they’re caught up in the writing.<br /><br />This is definitely one of my least favorite books. I’m glad I reread it, because finding these quotes and providing a more well researched review makes me feel a lot better. <b>I can only hope some others will see this review and recognize how many problematic tropes can be found in this book.</b><br /><br />Also, I think this is the longest review I’ve ever written. Considering my feelings on this book, I’m not surprised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5504504370906964422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_204068832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204068832" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204068832?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who don't mind the disturbing</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204068832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13221719694888771310"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b>. The fact is, this is my third read by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins' title='Ellen Hopkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ellen Hopkins</a> and all of the books I've read so far have affected me quite deeply. I've discovered in this past year that I really like novels in verse, I couldn't imagine it being my thing before I first picked up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/270807.Burned__Burned___1_' title='Burned (Burned, #1) by Ellen Hopkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Burned</a> but all the ones I've read have been all the more emotional, moving and effective because of it. Before I start on about what I don't like, I'll just say now: this book is worth your time if you are okay with the depressing, </span>
  <span id="freeText13221719694888771310" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b>. The fact is, this is my third read by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a> and all of the books I've read so far have affected me quite deeply. I've discovered in this past year that I really like novels in verse, I couldn't imagine it being my thing before I first picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/270807.Burned__Burned___1_" title="Burned (Burned, #1) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Burned</a> but all the ones I've read have been all the more emotional, moving and effective because of it. Before I start on about what I don't like, I'll just say now: this book is worth your time if you are okay with the depressing, disturbing and occasionally gross.<br><br>But, there's this one thing that is the same in all of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a>' books, and to understand it best try and imagine the novel is two halves. Not a first half and a second half but various different parts of the novel that either fall into half one or half two. Okay, now half one is like the very first Saw film: original, shocking, disturbing, horrifying but good as well because it's so different. Half two is like the rest of the Saw films put together.<br><br><b>Ellen Hopkins is Jigsaw and she wants to play a game...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358050i/709228.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Half two is made up of the parts that made me think "surely Ms Hopkins is going to give these poor little buggers a break now?" I mean, honestly, how many ways can you find to torture a person? In the same way that I quickly became tired of the Saw series and it's tendency to just keep inventing new and exciting ways to horrendously kill people, there were parts where I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a> went too far. This book was 666 pages long (ominous) but really didn't need to be, the story was good, the characters were interesting... everything else that happened was like seeing how bad their lives could possibly get.<br><br><b>In the words of Bruce Nolan: "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a> is a mean kid sitting on an ant hill with a magnifying glass..."</b><br><br>Let's take Tony. Tony was repeatedly raped by his mother's boyfriend, he runs away and ends up popping pills and trying his hand at prostitution in order to get by, he then attempts suicide and gets carted off to Aspen Springs Psychiatric Hospital. There the doctors try and re-connect him with his long-lost father but Tony's unsure of his sexuality and his dad's some uber-religious and homophobic nutter. What next for this poor kid? Like I wouldn't have felt sorry for him had he just been raped! <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2821144.Ellen_Hopkins" title="Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Ellen Hopkins</a> doesn't know when to stop, it's like "right, he's been abused, drugged up, prostituted, discriminated against... I know, give him diarrhea as well!"<br><br>This book would be great to read if you think your life's shit. No matter how bad it gets for you, these kiddies have it so much worse. And if you think your life's worse than this, I recommend writing to Hopkins as you'll probably feature in her next book.<br><br>It's not like it isn't good. Half number one is fantastic: well-written, interesting, moving, gritty. And I can handle disturbing, it can usually get me hooked. I just feel that Hopkins uses the shock factor too much and it becomes less believable because of it.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13221719694888771310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132272568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132272568" />
    <a title="Ebehi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2028906-ebehi"><img alt="Ebehi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449010535p2/2028906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132272568?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ebehi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ebehi" href="/user/show/2028906-ebehi">Ebehi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132272568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8743065471035207642">I started this book very excited. Firstly, the cover looked interesting, then I saw that the story was written in verse form and my excitement level went higher. Perhaps my expectations multiplied my disappointment. Halfway through the book, I was only reading because I had already started and wanted to finish what I had started. Now what to start with...<br/><br/>1. There were many times when I couldn't distinguish the voices of the three different protagonists. I would start a chapter from a new person'</span>
  <span id="freeText8743065471035207642" style="display:none">I started this book very excited. Firstly, the cover looked interesting, then I saw that the story was written in verse form and my excitement level went higher. Perhaps my expectations multiplied my disappointment. Halfway through the book, I was only reading because I had already started and wanted to finish what I had started. Now what to start with...<br /><br />1. There were many times when I couldn't distinguish the voices of the three different protagonists. I would start a chapter from a new person's perspective but I would have turn back to check whose perspective it was because I could have sworn that somebody else in the book had just said the exact same thing. This is definitely a big NO considering the characters are supposed to be very different people. Trying to "figure  out" was a phrase I heard too often.<br /><br />2. The main characters were too judgmental. I almost started banging my head against the wall each time one of them commented about how everyone else in the institution was crazy. I mean, Justin was considered crazy because he had strong religious beliefs. And for someone who claimed to believe in God, Tony was not cutting Justin any slack. Dahlia was constantly insulted even though they didn't really know her story. Lori was derided for being moody when, HELLO, most of them were on anti-depressants anyway because they were mostly DEPRESSED. All in all, the only impression I could get was that these were just regular kids with problems but the main characters were too concerned with forming weird love triangles and figuring each other out that they only took the time to gossip about everyone else. Vanessa didn't seem at all special or kind per se, so I don't understand why Tony and Conner were both so fixated on how pure and perfect she was. All she did was act anti-social with everyone else. And the only time she actually socialized was when she was insulting Dahlia.<br /><br />3. Their stories ended up not being very interesting. Only Tony's story seemed even remotely engaging. And for all the internal whining they did, and all the times when the story was cut off before some "big revelation" Conner didn't seem like anything more than any regular rich kid with not-overly-affectionate parents. It was never really addressed why he felt depressed enough to try to commit suicide over Emily, neither was why he hated Cara so much and called her a b***h. Vanessa didn't have much to tell either, and much of what was going on with her could be explained away because she was bipolar. And the way she would describe her dad as if she hated him, then as if he was the greatest person in the world was just very confusing.<br /><br />4. There were just too many oversexualized references in the book. Especially in places that they were not really necessary. <br /><br />5. The love thing was just strange. How can Tony, Vanessa, and Conner be sitting together in a bus full of people, and Tony starts kissing Vanessa and expects NO ONE to see. And no one actually sees? Except Conner. And for all their friendship, Tony and Vanessa are not considerate enough to keep their PDAs out of Conner's sight especially since he liked Vanessa too.<br /><br />6. All these, and more, make me so frustrated with the characters that I cannot really relate with them.<br /><br />One star for effort and emotion. But if she's writing in verse form, Hopkins should try to pay more attention to it because towards the end it just got sloppy as if she wrote really short prose then just arranged it in lines. <br /><br /><br />**********SPOILER ALERT*****************<br /><br />The whole Vanessa and abortion thing was just like WTF? I mean, is the HUGE secret she had been holding all this while? I didn't even really mesh with the rest of the story so far. And after the BIG REVELATION, it was never brought up again, as if mentioning it once was enough for Vanessa to get over it. Meh</span>
  <a data-text-id="8743065471035207642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228934241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228934241" />
    <a title="Megs ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5691412-megs"><img alt="Megs ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587306329p2/5691412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228934241?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megs ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megs ♥" href="/user/show/5691412-megs">Megs ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=favs">favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=z-2012-reads">z-2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5691412-megs?shelf=written-in-verse">written-in-verse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228934241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6809100538926173270"><br/><br/><i>Impulse</i> is a very short, but very powerful story.<br/><br/>Ellen Hopkins is known for tackling those tough issues that are shocking to read about, but are particularly more disturbing when they are about such young people. Three characters lives intersect at a mental health facility, and at first the story is mostly about each one and how they landed there. The story soon shifts gears, and it becomes more about the bond these characters created. We read on, wondering if they will be able to help each othe</span>
  <span id="freeText6809100538926173270" style="display:none"><br /><br /><i>Impulse</i> is a very short, but very powerful story.<br /><br />Ellen Hopkins is known for tackling those tough issues that are shocking to read about, but are particularly more disturbing when they are about such young people. Three characters lives intersect at a mental health facility, and at first the story is mostly about each one and how they landed there. The story soon shifts gears, and it becomes more about the bond these characters created. We read on, wondering if they will be able to help each other get on with their horrible lives. They all have their own story, but they have one thing in common. They all ended up in the facility after a botched suicide attempt. The I'm sorry to say that is about all I'm going to say about this book as far as plot is concerned. The beauty of this book is in turning each page and wondering what new bit of information is going to be revealed about each person's past.<br /><br />Ellen writes this book in verse, like several of her other books. I find her writing to be excellent. When other less skillful authors try to write about these difficult subjects they can often rely on stereotypes and cliches making the whole thing just feel wrong. Or they walk on eggshells around the subject hoping you will pull from it what they want you to, but you just end up feeling nothing, because proper explanations or details were never given. Ellen has skills, however, and you are most likely always going to have some sort of emotional reaction to her writing. Hopkins has said that her “books are not about the things that happen to…characters, but rather about how those characters react to those things.” I feel that definitely describes Impulse.<br /><br />I do feel like this book was a little too short, but I can't wait to read the sequel, Perfect.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who doesn't have problems reading about suicide, because honestly she doesn't hold anything back. If this is a touchy subject for you, you probably should avoid this book. For everyone else this is a tragic yet hopeful story that you will be thinking about long after you've read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6809100538926173270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_223845378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223845378" />
    <a title="Jude" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4418048-jude"><img alt="Jude" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483571062p2/4418048.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223845378?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jude" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jude" href="/user/show/4418048-jude">Jude</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223845378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4269248137792811020">It’s hard to review this book, it really is. Suicide is not something to be taken lightly, and it is also something very hard to grasp. Something that we usually tiptoe around, nobody wants to be that close to death. Ever. What makes it so shocking is to wonder: What can drive a person to such an ending? Why is it that they couldn’t see beyond their current situations, and why did they thought they had nothing left to loose.<br/><br/>It was especially hard for me to read this because I’ve been in this sor</span>
  <span id="freeText4269248137792811020" style="display:none">It’s hard to review this book, it really is. Suicide is not something to be taken lightly, and it is also something very hard to grasp. Something that we usually tiptoe around, nobody wants to be that close to death. Ever. What makes it so shocking is to wonder: What can drive a person to such an ending? Why is it that they couldn’t see beyond their current situations, and why did they thought they had nothing left to loose.<br><br>It was especially hard for me to read this because I’ve been in this sort of situation, think of me as Vanessa [If you have read the book] if not, well, you need to read it, you really do. Everything was so real, and I actually thought I was going to have trouble keeping up with the writing style, but no, it was really easy to follow and to get into it.<br><br><i>Impulse</i> shows the life of mainly three teens, though there are more people interned in Aspen Springs and you get to catch a glimpse of them. <i>Impulse</i> really shows this: Some people will make it. Others won’t. In school, in a marathon, in life, in anything you can think about. Some people aren’t strong enough. Some people don’t want to fight anymore. They all act on their Impulse.<br><br>A strong story that comes with stronger decisions. If you’ve read titles such as Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma or Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher, Impulse is a must-be in your shelf<br><br><a href="http://inbetweenwritingandreading.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342513i/698212.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1206109872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206109872" />
    <a title="Mary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17156965-mary"><img alt="Mary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427193557p2/17156965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206109872?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary" href="/user/show/17156965-mary">Mary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206109872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4456628634030989989"><b>THE GOOD:</b><br/><br/>* I’m really warming up to novels in verse, because I feel like they’re more introspective <br/>* I like that the author isn’t afraid to explore tough or sensitive issues and does so pretty straight forward<br/>* can you tell by my tone that I really struggled to find good things, because OH BOY<br/><br/><b>THE BAD:</b><br/><br/>* where even to start jesus h christ<br/>* so the mental health aspect was Poorly Handled™ (ps - this is an understatement) and romanticised - fyi, the plot takes place at a mental health facility<br/>* like</span>
  <span id="freeText4456628634030989989" style="display:none"><b>THE GOOD:</b><br /><br />* I’m really warming up to novels in verse, because I feel like they’re more introspective <br />* I like that the author isn’t afraid to explore tough or sensitive issues and does so pretty straight forward<br />* can you tell by my tone that I really struggled to find good things, because OH BOY<br /><br /><b>THE BAD:</b><br /><br />* where even to start jesus h christ<br />* so the mental health aspect was Poorly Handled™ (ps - this is an understatement) and romanticised - fyi, the plot takes place at a mental health facility<br />* like... look at this shit: <i>“I'll never stop cutting, lithium or no lithium. Only love can make me stop.“</i><br />* NO<br />* <i>“Vanessa and Tony—two fractured people, healed (perhaps) by unforeseen, not to mention unlikely, love."</i> - the characters who recover are the ones that fall in love and THIS IS SO WRONG I CANNOT<br />* the one gay character turns out not to be gay at the end? In his words: “My lifestyle has caused me a lot of pain. I hope to change that when I get out of here.” - just to be clear, he’s talking about his gay lifestyle. He was sexually assaulted, which led him to believe he was gay?? but hey, rejoice, he’s actually not????<br />* whyyyyyyyy is this happening - gay people aren’t gay because something bad happened to them, stoooooop this<br />* ALSO - suicide is basically treated like a plot device and in the end, one of the characters commits suicide so that the other two can basically be together without anyone interfering, at least that’s what I gathered out of it<br />* WHHYYYYYYYY<br />* there are so many sensitive issues crammed in, that at one point it doesn’t seem believable anymore: suicide (by several methods), self harm, drug abuse, sexual assault, sexual abuse, abortion, child neglect, AIDS, murder and others I’m not mentioning because I am Tired.<br />* this actually leads, imo, to poor character development and they just feel... like they’re there.; I couldn’t sympathise to any of them<br />* oversexualization - like, my dudes, it was painful at times<br />* this book is a Mess™<br />* like... no<br /><br /><b>YAY or NAY:</b> avoid it like the plague, but if you do decide to read it for yourself, be mindful of the crap<br /><br /><b>★</b></span>

<div id="review_1514750698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1514750698" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1514750698?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514750698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12730842062734085735"><b>***This is an old review. I did an in-depth analysis of this book during my second read. That review is much better! Link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918354321?book_show_action=false'>https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> ****</b><br/><br/>Trigger warning for every bad thing ever—and I mean EVERY bad thing! Please only pick this up if you are comfortable with seriously mature subject matter.<br/><br/><b>Also, semi-rant ahead. Be prepared.</b><br/><br/>This is another one of those books that I’m incredibly conflicted about. I started off confident that this was going to be a four star book, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText12730842062734085735" style="display:none"><b>***This is an old review. I did an in-depth analysis of this book during my second read. That review is much better! Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918354321?book_show_action=false">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> ****</b><br /><br />Trigger warning for every bad thing ever—and I mean EVERY bad thing! Please only pick this up if you are comfortable with seriously mature subject matter.<br /><br /><b>Also, semi-rant ahead. Be prepared.</b><br /><br />This is another one of those books that I’m incredibly conflicted about. I started off confident that this was going to be a four star book, but that slowly climbed down to a three, and then a two. <br /><br />Though two was my initial rating I've decided to lower it to a one after looking over my finished review. If I can write this long of a rant about a book it can only receive a one star.<br /><br />I read the companion novel to this book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917945.Perfect__Impulse___2_" title="Perfect (Impulse, #2) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect</a>, back in November for my book club. I thought it was well written, though I didn’t find it enjoyable due to it basically being A Series of Unfortunate Events: The R-Rated Version.<br /><br />The ending of <i>Perfect</i> threw me for such a loop that I felt like I just had to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/270805.Impulse__Impulse___1_" title="Impulse (Impulse, #1) by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Impulse</a> to see the story from the other side. <b>Sadly I liked <i>Perfect</i> a lot more,</b> due to the characters being much more likable and developed among other things.<br /><br /><i>Impulse</i> follows three characters, one of which is Conner, the twin brother of Cara from <i>Perfect</i> aka the reason why I picked up this book. The three main characters are living in treatment facility and each has attempted suicide.<br /><br />Typically I don’t pick up books that deal with such a heavy subject matter, but I think that every once in a while it’s good to set my fantasy aside and pick up something raw and real, like I was hoping <i>Impulse</i> to be.<br /><br /><b>Sadly I found <i>Impulse</i> to be one of the worst portrayals of mental illness I’ve ever read about.</b><br /><br />Gah, I had so many problems with this book, where do I even start? Let’s go through the main characters.<br /><br /><b>Conner:</b> I expected to really like Conner’s character from <i>Perfect</i>, but Imma be real here; Conner creeped me the fuck out. Was this intentional? Why did the author feel the need to turn a character that should have been sympathetic into a creep? He makes these weird sex references and metaphors and made me extremely uncomfortable, and it bordered on being perv-y.<br /><br /><b>Tony:</b> I liked Tony well enough throughout most of the book. He’s sympathetic and believable; he has an interesting story arc and is an overall good guy. My issue was with the way his sexuality was dealt with, but it’s a spoiler.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So at the beginning of the book Tony is confident in being gay and is open about his sexuality. By the end of the book Tony begins to start healing from the things in his life that caused him to attempt suicide, and it’s about at that time he realizes he isn’t gay and begins to “fall in love” with Vanessa. I know from the author’s other works that it was probably not her intention but <b>that sends an AWFUL message!</b> Tony finds his 'salvation' and begins to heal when he becomes straight? UM WHAT?! It sounds like she’s trying to say that real love is between heterosexual people, which I know wasn’t her intent but it most certainly came off that way. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Vanessa:</b> I felt absolutely no connection to her. Her chapters were boring and she was the most undeveloped of the group. Also Vanessa was kind of a mary sue special snowflake whatever, you know the type.<br /><br /><b>All of the characters kind of felt underdeveloped to me, which is weird since this book is 666 (*eye roll*) pages, plenty of time to develop your characters.</b> I remember really feeling like I knew the characters at the end of <i>Perfect</i>, but I never connected to or cared about any of these characters. Probably cuz they creeped me out, just sayin'.<br /><br />The “teens” didn’t sound like teens in the slightest. <b>Has Ellen Hopkins ever talked to a teen? I probably should have grabbed some quotes, but the way these kids talked was ridiculous.</b> I can’t picture anyone, let alone someone near my age, talking like these people. Maybe the constant sexual crap was her attempt at making them sound younger, but it did not have that effect on me at all.<br /><br /><b>This was another book that promises to be a hard hitting tale of mental illness, but it’s really just a disguise for an incredibly weird creepy romance and love triangle.</b><br /><br />Guys, when are going to stop romanticizing mental illness? <b>Love is NOT a cure for mental illness.</b> This book portrays treatment facilities in a bad light and the characters that recover recover through falling in love, but this is just not accurate.<br /><br /><b>The biggest issue for me was how oversexualized this was.</b> SO FREAKING OVERSEXUALIZED and it was not necessary at all. All these freaking kids talk about is sex, who they want to have sex with, metaphors about sex blah blah blah STOP. We get it, they’re supposed to be teenagers but my god. It made incredibly uncomfortable.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, I want to talk to the genius who said, “hey, let’s take all the suicidal teenagers hiking without harnesses on a cliff. I’M SURE THAT’LL GO FINE.” /facepalm <b>ARE YOU FUCKING KIDDING ME?! HOW IS THAT A GOOD IDEA?!</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Frankly I think Hopkins was more concerned about her story being shocking than being accurate in portraying mental illness.<br /><br />Sorry for the incredibly long review/rant, I just hate when a book dealing with heavy subject material like this disappoints. <b>Though they deal with very different subject matter I recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23848559.Furiously_Happy_A_Funny_Book_About_Horrible_Things" title="Furiously Happy A Funny Book About Horrible Things by Jenny Lawson" rel="nofollow noopener">Furiously Happy: A Funny Book About Horrible Things</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7893725.Hate_List" title="Hate List by Jennifer Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Hate List</a> for a book that portrays mental illness well.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12730842062734085735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40193926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40193926" />
    <a title="Kirsten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/821868-kirsten"><img alt="Kirsten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205553862p2/821868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40193926?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsten" href="/user/show/821868-kirsten">Kirsten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=children-or-ya">children-or-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40193926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13066762049361511071">This novel, written in free-verse poetry, is set at a mental institution and follows three teens who tried to commit suicide. Conner is a rich kid with a "perfect" life who tried to shoot himself. Vanessa, whose mother is also bipolar, is a cutter who went too far one day. And Tony, who lived on the street after being abused as a child, tried to kill himself with a drug overdose. Now they are all at a private mental hospital, trying to come to terms with what has brought them there.<br/><br/>I'd heard goo</span>
  <span id="freeText13066762049361511071" style="display:none">This novel, written in free-verse poetry, is set at a mental institution and follows three teens who tried to commit suicide. Conner is a rich kid with a "perfect" life who tried to shoot himself. Vanessa, whose mother is also bipolar, is a cutter who went too far one day. And Tony, who lived on the street after being abused as a child, tried to kill himself with a drug overdose. Now they are all at a private mental hospital, trying to come to terms with what has brought them there.<br /><br />I'd heard good things about Hopkins, but my ultimate reaction to this book was "bleh." I knew it was going to be a "problem novel," but I had hoped that Hopkins might do something interesting here. Instead, the characterization was often either flat (as in the case of Conner and his family) or full of holes (as in the case of Tony). Vanessa is the most well-fleshed-out character, but Hopkins leaves at least one major plot element just sort of dangling -- it's mentioned a few times, and then dropped. I suppose it might be in part due to the first-person nature of the narrative, but I was also disappointed by the way that Conner, Vanessa, and Tony seemed to be the only human characters in the novel. The other patients were characterized solely by their mental illnesses, and were very rarely treated with any kind of sympathy. I also didn't quite feel that Hopkins did a good enough job evoking the different voices of the main characters through the poetry, which was supposed to have been written by them: it all seemed as though it was written by the same person.<br /><br />I think this could be popular with upper middle and high school students, but it's likely to rub some more mature readers the wrong way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13066762049361511071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2190902165" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190902165" />
    <a title="chrissy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70647601-chrissy"><img alt="chrissy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190902165?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chrissy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chrissy" href="/user/show/70647601-chrissy">chrissy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to chrissy by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/70647554-faith">Faith</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70647601-chrissy?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70647601-chrissy?shelf=seventh-grade">seventh-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70647601-chrissy?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70647601-chrissy?shelf=format-hardcover">format-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70647601-chrissy?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190902165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7216507639902523831"><b><u>NOTE:</u> The more I think about this book, the more I realize how much I enjoyed reading this book, regardless of all of the below. While everything that I have written below is still accurate and should, and will, stay in this review, I honestly <i>really</i> enjoyed reading this book. Actually, at the time I am writing this review, I just rechecked this book out from my local public library, and I am going to start rereading it.</b><br/><br/><i>With the above in mind, please disregard anything that states such along the</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7216507639902523831" style="display:none"><b><u>NOTE:</u> The more I think about this book, the more I realize how much I enjoyed reading this book, regardless of all of the below. While everything that I have written below is still accurate and should, and will, stay in this review, I honestly <i>really</i> enjoyed reading this book. Actually, at the time I am writing this review, I just rechecked this book out from my local public library, and I am going to start rereading it.</b><br /><br /><i>With the above in mind, please disregard anything that states such along the lines of 'I hated this book' or 'I didn't like this book at all'. As I may have had problems with the book itself, I truly did enjoy reading it, as stated in the above blurb on more than one occasion. I would go back and rewrite this review, or at least edit it, but, quite frankly, I'm too lazy to do so at the moment. Who knows, I might do so down the road, but for right now, it's staying the same.</i><br /><br /><b>There are some <i>MINOR</i> unmarked spoilers scattered throughout this review</b><br /><br />It's no surprise that Hopkins is pretty much known for tackling a lot of hard, serious topics in her books, but she went overboard with the number of them in <i>Impulse</i>. The main ones being <b>suicide, but not just one or two kinds of suicide, but three -- pills, blades, guns</b> -- along with <b>mental health facilities</b>. In addition, there are a lot of others such as <b>schizophrenia, bipolar disorder, parental abuse, parental suicide, molestation, any drug you can name is probably mentioned <i>somewhere</i> in this book, cutting, abortion</b>, and those are just <u>some</u> of the <b>main</b> ones. I could give you my longest Goodreads review listing the issues she attempted to tackle, but I want to make this at least somewhat entertaining, so I'm stopping there. <b>Nobody who tries to tackle THAT many issues in one single novel is going to do it well</b>.<br /><br />All of Hopkins' books, for the most part, revolve around teenagers, which I find ironic considering she had literally <b>NO</b> idea how teenagers <i>actually</i> talk in <i>Impulse</i>. On what world would a teenager who was <i>not even one page before</i> talking about his girlfriend having an orgasm describe his own mother as, <i>...an ice princess mom who raised me with glass kisses</i>. <br /><br />Not to mention, while we were on the topic of how Hopkins failed to represent teens well in <i>Impulse</i>, there is so much talk about love and sex to the point where it all feels way too oversexualized. Apparently, to Hopkins, all teenagers want is sex, which, while true for some, is not accurate for all teenagers. <br /><br />Hopkins used love basically as a cure for mental illness. <i>I'll never stop cutting, lithium or no lithium. Only love can make me stop</i>. I'm not a genius or anything, but I'm pretty damn sure love can't magically cure depression and stop a person from cutting. <br /><br />In the end, Conner's suicide is used essentially just so Vanessa and Tony can get together. I know the whole idea of the book is that three teenagers become teens who tried to commit suicide, but suicide is more or less just used a plot device. The whole sh*tty love triangle theme throughout nonetheless just made me angry and annoyed the entire time I was reading. I couldn't ignore it, either, as the entire story, for the most part, revolves around the love triangle, which, in the long run, leads Conner to suicide.<br /><br />Probably the most problematic thing I have <u>EVER</u> read was regarding Tony's sexuality throughout this book. Tony essentially realizes that is only gay due to him previously being sexually abused so then he "turns straight". <br /><br /><b>Listen.</b> I don't like this AT ALL because it nonetheless implies that all gays are gay because something has happened to them and something is wrong with them. <i>That is <b>NOT</b> the case whatsoever</i>! It also insinuates that Tony has to be straight or else he won't recover and leave Aspen Springs. <br /><br />I don't know if there is anything I hate more than when I am reading a book where the main setting is a mental health facility and the mental health facility is represented in an inaccurate way. A lot of teens who read books such as <i>Impulse</i> are going through something similar and that is why they choose to read it. Because of that, it is important for the book to accurately represent mental health facilities. Hopkins sets up a bad relationship between the teens and their therapists by implying they are bad people. I think there was <i>maybe</i> one adult in this novel who <b>wasn't</b> portrayed as evil, horrible people.<br /><br />I liked the idea of having the levels that they advance to until they thought it would be a good idea to take <b>FORMAL SUICIDAL TEENAGERS on the side of a f**king cliff</b>. Yeah, because basically gifting teens who had once attempted to commit suicide an opportunity to kill themselves by taking them hiking on the side of a cliff where they could jump any second is a good idea when the whole idea of the levels is to advance them until they prove themselves as "healthy". It just doesn't make any sense to me??<br /><br />I thought all three of the characters were nonetheless underdeveloped and kind of <i>bland</i>. There were several times where I had to flip back a couple pages to refresh whos perspective I was reading because they all blended together to me even though, after the first 50 pages, I figured out every six pages was a new perspective and they always went in the same order. <br /><br />I also didn't understand the whole secret revelation of Vanessa's abortion. It felt so out of place as it didn't flow or mesh with anything else in the story, not to mention, that it was brought up within the last like 60 pages or so and never mentioned again. It seemed unnecessary to me, to be honest.<br /><br /><b>The conclusion will be rewritten at a later date, as stated in the second little blurb at the very top/beginning of this review.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7216507639902523831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      A friend

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>,
